Jamison Brereton

96 (705)
Indra (except Maruts 14d, Indra and Br╠еhaspati 15)
Tira┼Ыc─л ─Ас╣Еgirasa or Dyut─Бna M─Бruti
21 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh except vir─Бj 4, arranged in trcas ╠е
A rich and complex hymn containing both glancing references and vivid treatments of several Indra myths. Its parts conform well to the tr╠еca structure, especially (as often) toward the end. Each of the last four tr╠еcas (vss. 10тАУ21) has a verbal signa ture: in verses 10тАУ12 the half-p─Бda refrain тАЬsurely he will take cognizanceтАЭ (kuv├нd aс╣Еga╠Б ve╠Бdat); in verses 13тАУ15 the тАЬdropletтАЭ (drapsa╠Б); in verses 16тАУ18 the opening тАЬyou
thenтАЭ (tuva╠Бс╣Г ha tya╠Бd); in verses 19тАУ21 the definitional тАЬVr╠еtra-smiterтАЭ (vr╠еtrah─Б╠Б). The first tr╠еca of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ3) sets the stage for the wide-ranging praise of Indra by describing his overwhelming power in three different areas. In verse 1 the powers of nature are subject to him. Verse 2 apparently contains a snatch of the Emuс╣гa myth, most extensively related in VIII.71. In that myth Indra shoots a boar named Emuс╣гa through many mountains; here only the mountains and the arrow-shot are mentioned, but the prodigious nature of the unnamed archerтАЩs action is clear, and the audience would be aware that this was a boyhood deed of IndraтАЩs. In verse 3 IndraтАЩs body is described as the site of his powers, both physical and mental.
The second tr╠еca (vss. 4тАУ6) begins with a summary of his preeminence (vs. 4), but soon moves to the Vr╠еtra battle (vs. 5) and especially to the MarutsтАЩ role in it, a topic that will also occupy the third tr╠еca. The Maruts appear to be the тАЬformula torsтАЭ (brahm├бns) introduced at the end of verse 5, bellowing to Indra. Verses 6тАУ9 are best interpreted as the direct speech of the Maruts to Indra, offering him their praise while seeking an alliance with him. They remind him (vs. 7) that they stuck and continue to stick by him when the other gods deserted him in the Vr╠еtra battle, and they put in their claim to share the sacrifice with him (vs. 8), a claim also vividly dramatized in the dialogue hymn I.165. They end their speech (vs. 9) with the reas
surance that together they, the Maruts and Indra, will make an unbeatable team. The next tr╠еca (vss. 10тАУ12) returns to the ritual present, with the poetтАЩs exhorta tion to himself to produce well-crafted words for IndraтАФwhose attention to the praises he nervously hopes for. The following tr╠еca (vss. 13тАУ15) is the most puz zling part of the hymn; it concerns an otherwise unknown story about a тАЬdropletтАЭ (draps├б) or perhaps an individual (human? divine? semi-divine?) so named. There is a conflict of some sort in the Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л River, which Indra appears to win in verse 15. The middle verse of the tr╠еca (vs. 14) is 1st-person direct speech and may be the

words of Indra addressing the Maruts. But the тАЬstoryтАЭ may also be an extended ritual metaphor. тАЬDropletтАЭ is a word also used of soma, and the name of the river means literally тАЬpossessing (soma) plants.тАЭ The descent of the droplet into the river could well describe the rinsing of the soma plant that forms a regular part of soma preparation, although the ritual counterpart of the mythic conflict is difficult to identify.
Unified by its opening words тАЬyou then,тАЭ the next tr╠еca (vss. 16тАУ18) provides a survey of some of IndraтАЩs great deeds, some obscure (like the rivalry with the unidentified seven in vs. 16), some familiar: the defeat of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa (17c), the release of the cows from Vala (17d), and the Vr╠еtra battle again (18). The last tr╠еca begins with a riddle, though not a very challenging one. The first three p─Бdas of verse 19 give a series of definitional descriptors of a hero. Those asked the riddle give their answer to тАЬthe other,тАЭ in our opinion the riddler himself: тАЬThatтАЩs the Vr╠еtra-smiter!тАЭ And they provide other embellishments to the Vr╠еtra-smiter in the following two verses (20тАУ21), while declaring the need to invoke and praise him. The hymn thus keeps returning to the Vr╠еtra battle, and the final three verses implicitly assert that Vr╠еtra-smiter is IndraтАЩs fundamental role.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFor him the dawns prolonged their rising; for Indra the nights uttered auspicious voices by night; for himthe waters, the mothers, the seven rivers, stood, offering an easy passage for men to cross over.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The nightsuttered auspicious voices by night: All men read the Veda, etc. in the latter half of the night; therefore, the voicesof the night were auspicious; they studied the Veda under Indra’s direction

Jamison Brereton

For him do the dawns pass along their course; for Indra do the eloquent evenings (pass along their course) by night.
For him do the waters, the seven mothers, stand stillтАФthe rivers easy to cross, for men to traverse.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The relative phrase y─Б╠Бс╕е тАж bh├║jaс╕е тАЬwhich delightful thingsтАЭ has no obvious correlative expression in the main clause of cd. Geldner supplies тАЬ(mit denen),тАЭ which is certainly possible and perhaps the default option. But following a suggestion of OldenbergтАЩs, I take the asya of c, otherwise unaccounted for, as the functional correlative, despite the difference in number and gender. Because it is unaccented, asya should be pronominal and refer to something already present in the discourse, and there are few candidates, esp. because stot├бr- doesnтАЩt seem to take a genitive. It would not be surprising to resume the fem. expression тАЬdelightful thingsтАЭ simply with тАЬthat (stuff).тАЭ The masc. singular referring to the goods Indra has acquired continues in vs. 2, with the y├бm тАж t├бm pair. I tr. asya тАЬfrom thatтАЭ rather than тАЬof that,тАЭ since the latter doesnтАЩt parse well in English.

In cd stot─Б╠Бram тАж y├й ca тАж vс╣Ыkt├бbarhiс╣гaс╕е is a nice example of the тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction.

Griffith

FOR him the Mornings made their courses longer, and Nights with pleasant voices spake to Indra.
For him the Floods stood still, the Seven Mothers, Streams easy for the heroes to pass over.

Geldner

F├╝r ihn hielten die Morgenr├╢ten ihr Kommen, f├╝r Indra die lobesamen N├дchte, die Nachtzeit richtig ein. Ihm standen die sieben m├╝tterlichen Gew├дsser still, die leicht zu durchschreitenden Fl├╝sse f├╝r die M├дnner zum Durchschreiten.

Grassmann

Es bahnten ihm den Weg die Morgenr├╢then, bei Nacht dem Indra die gepries’nen Sterne, Die sieben M├╝tter standen ihm, die Wasser, zur Fahrt den M├дnnern, Str├╢me leicht durchfahrbar.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy him the thrower, unaided, were pierced asunder the thrice seven table-lands of the mountainheaped together; neither god nor mortal could do what he, the showerer, in his full-grown strength has done.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pierced asunderthe thrice seven tablelands: the legend in RV 8.8.10

Jamison Brereton

They were pierced through by the archer, though he waveredтАФthe thrice seven backs of the mountains fitted firmly together.
No god nor mortal could surpass thisтАФ(the deeds) that the bull, grown strong, performed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. ├бvyayam as тАШohne EinbusseтАЩ (loss), rather than тАШovine, belonging to sheepтАЩ (contra Grassmann, etc.), presumably because of its initial accent (against the normal accent in avy├бya- тАШovineтАЩ). This seems unnecessary. The other occurrence of ├бvyaya- (IX.86.34) modifies the soma filter and Geldner renders it тАЬaus SchafwolleтАЭ without comment. In our passage he is following S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs vyayarahitam, but vyaya- тАШdisappearance, loss, outlayтАЩ is not attested until the epic/Classical language, as far as I know. Furthermore, sheep fit nicely into this equine and bovine context, with the three terms ├б┼Ыvaс╣Г g─Б╠Бm bh─Бg├бс╣Г ├бvyayam displaying a classic BehagelтАЩs Law configuration. As for the aberrant accent, Debrunner (AiG II.2.213) attributes it to the influence of semantically identical ├бvya-.

Geldner takes the locative phrase in c with ab, тАЬWelches Ross und Rind du тАж als Anteil тАж bestimmt hat f├╝r den Opfernden тАжтАЭ Again this seems odd and unnecessary.

The locatives of c are summarized by t├бsmin in d, and contrast with paс╣Зa├║ at the end of that p─Бda. Moreover the middle voice of dadhiс╣г├й in the relative clause contrasts functionally with the act. imperative dhehi in the main clause. First Indra acquires goods for himself, then confers them on others. By placing the recipient in the rel.

clause with the middle verb, Geldner erases this neat voice contrast. P─Бda c then seems to represent a heavy preposed NP picked up by initial t├бsmin in d.

Griffith

The Darter penetrated, though in trouble, thrice-seven close-pressed ridges of the mountains.
Neither might God nor mortal man accomplish what the Strong Hero wrought in full-grown vigour.

Geldner

Der Sch├╝tze, obwohl er ohne festen Halt war, hat die dreimal sieben festgef├╝gten R├╝cken der Berge durch und durch geschossen. Das w├╝rde kein Gott oder Sterblicher ├╝berbieten, was alles der ausgewachsene Bulle getan hat.

Grassmann

Durchbohrt vom Sch├╝tzen sind, auch wenn er taumelt, die dreimal sieb’n vereinten Bergesgipfel; Kein Sterblicher, kein Gott vermag zu st├╢ren die Werke, die der hohe Stier vollbracht hat.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra’s iron thunderbolt is grasped firmly in his hand, enormous strength resides in his arms; when hegoes forth (to battle), there is ample employment for his head and his mouth, and (his followers) rush near him tohear his commands.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ample employment for his head and his mouth: i.e. his head is employed in fitting thehelmet, etc., and his eyes in seeking the enemy; and the mouth issues its various orders

Jamison Brereton

The metal mace is an appendage of Indra; greatest power is in the two arms of Indra.
The intentions of Indra are in his head exclusively; into his mouth they rush en masse, to (become speech) worthy to be heard.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the doubling of pres. s├бsti тАШsleepsтАЩ with the adverbial gerund anuс╣гv─Б╠Бpam. In Jamison 1982/83 I argue that the gerund is used here because the poet wanted to use a pres. tense of тИЪsvap but didnтАЩt really know one, since the various presents to this root are secondary and to some extent improvisational.

The end of the verse тАж dhehi t├бс╣Г t├бtaс╕е with its two final pronominals is striking, but clearly constructed as the mirror image of 2d t├бsminn t├бс╣Г dhehi. The good sacrificer of 2cd is contrasted with the godless, vowless man of 3, and it may not be entirely fanciful to suggest that the unusual word order тАФ t├б-forms ordinarily occurring at the beginning of clauses тАФ is a syntactic expression of his perverse nature.

Griffith

The mightiest force is Indra’s bolt of iron when firmly grasped in both the arms of Indra.
His head and mouth have powers that pass all others, and all his people hasten near to listen.

Geldner

Dem Indra ist die eherne Keule anh├дnglich, in Indra┬┤s Armen ist die meiste St├дrke. Ausschlie├Яlich in Indra┬┤s Haupt sind die Gedanken. An seinen Mund r├╝cken sie dicht heran, um seinen Worten zu lauschen.

Grassmann

Des Indra Blitz, der eherne, er schmiegt sich an Indra’s Arme, und die h├╢chste St├дrke; In Indra’s Haupt ist Weisheit, ihm zu eigen, zum Munde drangen ein die sch├╢nen Tr├дnke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI think you the most worthy among those worthy of sacrifice; I think you the overthrower of theimperishable (mountains); I think you, Indra, the banner of warriors; I think you the showerer (of blessings) tomen.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Of the imperishable mountains: of the heroes not to be overthrown; banner of warriors: the manifester ofthyself to your worshippers

Jamison Brereton

I consider you the most worthy of the sacrifice of those worthy of the sacrifice; I consider you the stirrer of the unstirrable;
I consider you the beacon of warriors, Indra; I consider you the bull of the settled domains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Following Geldner I take ke┼Ы├нbhiс╕е тАЬhairy-maned (horses)тАЭ as an appositional simile with g─лrbh├нс╕е: the hymns serve as the team that brings Indra to us along тАЬheavenтАЩs way.тАЭ This latter form, dyug├бt тАШheaven-goingтАЩ vel sim., is extensively discussed by Scarlatta (106-7), who ultimately concludes that it is тАЬunklar,тАЭ though he favors taking it as a nom. sg. modifying the soma presser (sut─Б╠Бv─Бn). This seems odd: the somapresser is the one element in this verse who is likely to stay put. I take it, with Grassmann and (implicitly) Oldenberg, as adverbial, referring to the movement of the hymns, as metaphorical horses, through heaven. In his note Geldner endorses S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs interpretation of it is a shortening of dyug├бdbhiс╕е, which (as WolffтАЩs suggestion) Oldenberg dismisses without argument. This explanation by truncation certainly does not seem necessary, since a neuter adverb works well enough.

Griffith

1 count thee as the Holiest of the Holy, the caster-down of what hath ne’er been shaken.
I count thee as the Banner of the heroes, I count thee as the Chief of all men living.

Geldner

Ich halte dich f├╝r den Opferw├╝rdigen unter den Opferw├╝rdigen, ich halte dich f├╝r den Ersch├╝tterer der Unersch├╝tterlichen. Ich halte dich, Indra, f├╝r das Banner der Krieger, Ich halte dich f├╝r den Bullen der V├╢lker.

Grassmann

Dich halt’ ich f├╝r den Heiligen der Heil’gen, f├╝r den Beweger dich des Unbewegten; Dich halt’ ich, Indra, f├╝r das wahre Banner, dich f├╝r den Herrscher aller Menschenst├дmme.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Indra, you grasp in your arms your pride humbling thunderbolt to smite Ahi, when the mountainclouds loudly roar and the cows loudly bellow, then the br─Бhmaс╣Зas offer their worship to Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cows: cowsare the waters pent within the clouds;

Br─Бhmaс╣Зas = the mountains

Jamison Brereton

When, o Indra, in your two arms you took the mace stirred by
exhilaration, to smite the serpent,
the mountains bellowed forth, and forth the cows, forth the formulators [=Maruts] approaching Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verbal counterpart to 2nd sg. dhats├й in the relative cl. (ab) is augmented ├бnavanta in the main clause (cd). I would therefore prefer to take dhats├й as a medial, preterital perfect, rather than as a present. Grassmann and Lu identify it as present, Geldner translates it as one, and K├╝mmel (p. 275) explicitly claims that -i-liaison forms belong to the perfect, while those without the -i- are presents. Nonetheless, I think we can interpret dhats├й, the only such 2nd sg., as a perfect, next to very common dadhiс╣г├й, esp. as only this form would fit in a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence.

The accent on main-clause ├бnavanta must result from its membership in the repeated pr├б subclauses.

I take the formulators in d as the Maruts; Geldner suggests either Aс╣Еgirases or Maruts. Since the next tс╣Ыca (vss. 7-9) clearly contains the 1st ps. speech of the Maruts, and the next verse (6) has 1st ps. speech that can reasonably attributed to the Maruts, their introduction here would not be surprising.

Griffith

What time, O Indra, in thine arms thou tookest thy wildly rushing bolt to Slay the Dragon,
The mountains roared, the cattle loudly bellowed, the Brahmans with their hymns drew nigh to Indra.

Geldner

Wenn du, Indra, die Keule in die Arme nimmst, die rauscherregte, um den Drachen zu erschlagen, da schrieen die Berge auf, die K├╝he, die Hohenpriester, zu Indra kommend:

Grassmann

Als, Indra, du den Blitz in deinen Arm nahmst, den ungest├╝men, zu der Schlang’ Erlegung, Da jauchzten laut die Berge, laut die K├╝he, und laut die Beter, zu dem Indra dringend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us praise that Indra who produced all the things, to him all beings are subsequent; may we maintainfriendship with Indra by our hymns, let us bring the showerer (of blessings) near us by our praises.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May wemaintain friendship: mitram = maitr─лm; let us say by our hymns, may we be friends with Indra

Jamison Brereton

[Maruts:] тАЬLet us praise him, who begat all these creatures here
below him.
We would like to establish an alliance with Indra with our hymns; we would come near the bull with reverences.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (so also Grassmann) takes ├бvar─Бс╣Зy asm─Бt as temporal: тАЬdie nach ihm kommen,тАЭ whereas I interpret it spatially. Though тАЬlater than himтАЭ is possible, it seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++, in that if Indra begat them, they would have to be later than him. The idea is rather that they exist here on earth, below him,, and also that he begot them as subordinates. Cf. vrj├бnem ╠е ─Б╠Бvar─Бс╣Зi тАЬthese communities here belowтАЭ (IX.96.7) and b├бndh┼лm╠Рr im─Б╠Бm╠Р├бvar─Бn тАЬthese bonds here belowтАЭ (IX.97.17), which both seem spatial, not temporal, also.

Griffith

Let us praise him who made these worlds and creatures, all things that after him sprang into being.
May we win Mitra with our songs, and Indra, and. wait upon our Lord with adoration.

Geldner

Ihn wollen wir preisen, der alle diese Gesch├╢pfe erzeugt hat, die nach ihm kommen. Mit Indra m├╢chten wir Freundschaft schlie├Яen durch Lobesworte; wir wollen uns unter Verbeugungen zu dem Bullen setzen.

Grassmann

Ihn lasst uns preisen, welcher diese Wesen zusammt erschuf, die nach ihm sind entsprossen, Mit Indra lasst den Mitra uns verehren, mit Liedern uns in Demuth nah’n dem Helden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll the gods who were your friends forsook you, flying away at the snorting of Vс╣Ыtra; O Indra, let therebe friendship to you with the Maruts; then do you conquer all these hostile armies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Friendshi: (AitareyaBr─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.20): The Maruts alone did not leave him

Jamison Brereton

[Maruts:] тАЬShrinking from the hissing of Vr╠еtra, all the gods who were your partners deserted you.
Let your partnership be with the Maruts, Indra. Then you will win all these battles here.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

I have chosen to read the impv. bh├бv─Б in b with the two small clauses in c as well, though it is certainly possible to interpret those with Geldner as straight indicative nominal clauses: тАЬyou (are) there with help тАж; you (are) friendship тАжтАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The da capo-like structure of the verses in this tс╣Ыca, with the first p─Бda repeated verbatim as the last one, is quite unusual.

Griffith

Flying in terror from the snort of Vrtra, all Deities who were thy friends forsook thee.
So, Indra, be thy friendship with the Maruts: in all these battles thou shalt be the victor.

English translation:

тАЬThese sixty-three Maruts were worthy of sacrifice nourishing your vigour like cows gathered together;we come to you, do you grant us our portion; so will we produce strength in you by this offering.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thesesixty-three Maruts: triс╕е ┼Ыaс╣гс╣нiс╕е = thrice sixty; or, sixty-three; these were the nine companies of the Maruts, eachcomposed of seven. ┼Ъukla Yajus. 17.81-86 enumerates six companies of seven each; Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б1.5.11: saptagaс╣З─Б vai Marut─Бс╕е; another gaс╣Зa is to be sought in another ┼Ы─Бkh─Б; or in a khila; cf. Taittir─лya─Аraс╣Зyaka 4.24.25 for three gaс╣Зas

Jamison Brereton

[Maruts:] тАЬWe, the thrice sixty Maruts, having increased you as ruddy throngs [=herds of cattle] increase, are deserving of the sacrifice.
We reverently approach you. Make a share for us. We would honor
your unbridled force with this oblation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the med. pf. of тИЪvс╣Ыdh is ordinarily intransitive or reflexive, v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е is here best interpreted as transitive in the frame (тАЬincreasing you,тАЭ with tv─Б in a as obj.) but intransitive in the simile (тАЬas ruddy throngs increase,тАЭ with the nominative NP usr─Б╠Бiva r─Б┼Ы├бyaс╕е). See X.78.8 for a similar example of case disharmony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The da capo-like structure of the verses in this tс╣Ыca, with the first p─Бda repeated verbatim as the last one, is quite unusual.

Griffith

Thrice-sixty Maruts, waxing strong, were with thee, like piles of beaming light, worthy of worship.
We come to thee: grant us a happy portion. Let us adore thy might with this oblation.

Geldner

Zu dir kommen wir dreiundsechzig Marut wie die Kuhherden zunehmend, wir Opferw├╝rdige nahen dir. Bestimme uns einen Anteil; wir wollen deinem Mut mit diesem Opfer huldigen.

Grassmann

Dir folgen dreimal sechzig starke Maruts, ehrw├╝rdige, wie morgendliche Sterne; Wir gehn dich an, o schenk uns Gl├╝ckesgabe, wir huld’gen deiner Kraft mit diesem Opfer.

English translation:

тАЬYour sharp bow, the host of Maruts, and your thunderbolt who, Indra, has ever withstood? The asurasare weaponless and abandoned by the gods, drive them away by your discus, O с╣Ъj─лс╣гin.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cf. RV. 8.86.4

Jamison Brereton

[Maruts:] тАЬSharp is the weapon, the vanguard of the Maruts. (And) who dares venture against your mace, Indra?
The lords lacking gods are weapon-less. With your wheel [=discus?]
scatter them, possessor of the silvery drink.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

However tempting it might be, the juxtaposed phrase ├бsur─Б adev─Б╠Бс╕е is most likely not to be interpreted as an early instantiation of the Asura/Deva conflict of middle Vedic times. Instead it probably refers to human or semi-divine lords (for the former see W. E. Hale, 1986: 83) who do not have the gods on their side. Hale points out that adev├б- is the only form in the RV so accented (contrasting with ├бdeva-), and it must be a bahuvr─лhi meaning тАЬnot having gods, without gods.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSend forth an excellent hymn to great (Indra), the strong, might and most fortunate, (that he mayprosper) my cattle; utter many praises to Indra who is borne by praise, may he speedily give much wealth to me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who is borne by praise: cf. RV 1.30.5; 61.4

Jamison Brereton

For the great, strong, powerful one, for the one most propitious to cattle send forth a well-twisted (hymn).
Produce many hymns for Indra whose vehicle is songs, for his body.
Surely he will take cognizance (of them)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although they belong to different tс╣Ыcas, 10ab responds to vs. 9: in both Indra is characterized by the lexeme abh├н тИЪbh┼л тАШdominate, surmountтАЩ (9c abhibh┼л╠Бс╕е, 10a abhibh┼л╠Бtaram), with each governing an NP beginning with v├н┼Ыva-. Moreover, in vs. 9 it is said that gods (as well as mortals) have not attained (─Б┼Ыata) Indra, while in 10ab the gods appear to be the implied subject of the verbs tatakс╣гuс╕е and jajanuс╕е тАЬfashioned and begotтАЭ - in other words, paradoxically, though they do not attain him they are credited with creating him.

In c there is pseudo-etymological play between v├бriс╣гс╣нс╕еaс╣Г v├бre, which not only are unrelated but also belong to two different NPs, despite their adjaceny. There is some uncertainty about the position of ut├б or even what it is conjoining. Klein (DGRV I.346, 349) considers the p─Бda an XY ut├б construction, joining the two complex NPs that precede it, with the adjectives in d тАЬmerely strung on to the basical phrasal syntagmтАЭ (346).

The etymological figure ugr├бm ├│jiс╣гс╣нham, with a positive and its superlative, is reminiscent of the simplex followed by comparative in 9c / 10a abhibh┼л╠Бс╕е тАж abhibh┼л╠Бtaram. The rest of p─Бda d, tav├бsam tarasv├нnam, almost mimics an etymological figure via phonological scrambling, although the words are of course unrelated.

Griffith

To him the Strong and Mighty, most auspicious, send up the beAuteous hymn for sake of cattle.
Lay oa his body many songs for Indra invoked with song, for will not he regard. them?

Geldner

Dem Gro├Яen, Gewaltigen, Starken sende ein Loblied hinaus, der dem Zugtier gar freundlich ist! Bringe dem Indra f├╝r seine Person viele Lobesworte dar, den die Lobesworte anziehen. Gewi├Я wird er sie recht verstehen.

Grassmann

Dem grossen, hehren, starken sende Loblied, und Heerden treibe hin zum heilbegabten, Dem Liederfreunde lege viele Lieder ans Herz, dem Indra, ob er wol drauf achtet?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSend forth your praise to mighty Indra who is borne by hymns, as (a sailor sends a traveller) in a shipacross the rivers; bring to me by your rites that wealth which belongs to him renowned and beneficent; may hespeedily give much wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: Indra, aided by Bс╣Ыhaspati and the Maruts, slew the asura Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, who with10,000 other asuras had occupied the river Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л, which is said to be the Yamun─Б. Another legend fromBс╣Ыhaddevat─Б: Soma, being afraid of Vс╣Ыtra, took refuge with the Kurus by the river Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л. Indra followed itwith Bс╣Ыhaspati and the Maruts and begged it to return. It however refused, and attempted to resist; but it wasultimately conquered and carried back to the gods, who drank it and in consequence, vanquished the demonс╣гDraps = a common word for Soma, the dropping; or, swift-moving;

Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л = sunlight

Jamison Brereton

To him whose vehicle is hymns, to the far-ranging one send an inspired thought like (a boat) to the far shore of rivers with a wooden
(paddle).
Stroke the body of the famous, very enjoyable one with a visionary
thought. Surely he will take cognizance (of it)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is phonetic play between asvaran (a; see also abhisv├бr─Б 1b) to тИЪsvar тАШsoundтАЩ and s u var(-pati)(c) containing the тАШsunтАЩ word, although the latter of course has a distracted sv cluster.

Griffith

To him, the Mighty, who accepts laudation, send forth thy thought as by a boat o’er rivers,
Stir with thy hymn the body of the Famous and Dearest One, for will not he regard it?

Beweg’ das Lied dem starken Spruch-empf├дnger wie mit dem Ruder ├╝ber Flut der Str├╢me; Ber├╝hr den Leib des hehren mit Gebeten, des sehr willkommnen, ob er wol drauf achtet?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPerform those rites of yours that Indra may accept them; praise him to whom praise belongs, worshiphim with your service; O priest, adorn thyself, grieve not (for poverty); let Indra hear your praise, may he speedilygive much wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Labor at what Indra will enjoy from you. Give as praise a good praise hymn. Seek to entice him here with reverence.
Be attentive, singer. DonтАЩt screech, but make your speech heard. Surely he will take cognizance (of it)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

I use two different English tr. for namanti, тАШbendтАЩ and тАШbowтАЩ, depending on the object; this is merely an English problem, as the passage adduced by Geldner shows: VII.23.20 ─Б╠Б… ├нndram … name gir─Б╠Б, nem├нс╣Г t├бс╣гс╣нeva.

In cd I supply тАШcry outтАЩ (тИЪsvar) on the basis of 11a s├бm тАж asvaran (note the s├бm in 12d) and 12b (abhi)sv├бr─Б.

Geldner takes tarasv├нnaс╕е as nom. pl., which is grammatically possible, but I prefer OldenbergтАЩs gen. sg. (an alternative also for Grassmann), since the same adj. modifies Indra in 10d.

Griffith

Serve him with gifts of thine which Indra welcomes: praise with fair praise, invite him with thine homage.
Draw near, O singer, and refrain from outcry. Make thy voice heard, for will not he regard it?

Geldner

Bring das fertig, woran dir Indra Gefallen finden wird, sing ein Loblied, bitte ihn unter Verbeugungen her! Mach deine Sache recht, o S├дnger, gr├╢le nicht, la├Я deine Rede h├╢ren! Gewi├Я wird er sie recht verstehen.

Grassmann

Das bringe dar, was gern dir Indra annimmt, das Loblied singe, lock ihn her durch Andacht; Hab’ Acht, o S├дnger, nicht sei rauh die Stimme; das Lied lass h├╢ren, ob er wol drauf achtet?

English translation:

тАЬThe swift-moving Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa with ten thousand (demons) stood on the Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л; by his might Indracaught him snorting (in the water); he, benevolent to man, smote his malicious (bands).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Droplet descended into the Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л (River),
the black one speeding with the ten thousand.
Indra with his skill helped him as he blew.
The manly minded one repelled the тАЬblizzardsтАЭ (of attacking warriors?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ca in c is one of the rare examples of subordinating ca in the RV, as shown by the accent induced on the verb vav├бrtat; see Klein DGRV I.240-41. Its position, about which Klein does not comment, is peculiar, but it can probably be accounted for metrically. In this particular Atijagat─л line (13 syl.), there is a natural break after the first two words (5 syllables), m├бс╣Гhiс╣гс╣нho g─лrbh├нr, and the rest of the line behaves as if it were a dimeter (8-syl.) line, ─Б╠Бca yaj├▒├нyo vav├бrtat, with initial preverb followed by the enclitic conjunction.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the introduction, the identity of the тАШdropletтАЩ (draps├б-) and the purport of this tс╣Ыca are quite unclear. Geldner takes both draps├б- and kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├б- (тАШblackтАЩ) as PNs and the tс╣Ыca as their тАЬsaga.тАЭ Since such a saga is otherwise unknown and both words have lexical meaning, such an approach does not seem to gain us much.

OldenbergтАЩs discussion is, as usual, very sharp, but his own interpretation, that Indra is helping an embryonic version of Bс╣Ыhaspati, in the form of a drop of semen, to come to birth, also does not convince.

Schmidt (1968: 112-13) rejects OldenbergтАЩs interpretation and suggests that it describes in mystical fashion the freeing of the soma-drop in the form of the sun, but declines to tr. the tс╣Ыca because of the many uncertainties.

I am inclined to see it as a treatment of the ritual step of rinsing the soma in water, as I said in the published introduction, though much remains murky.

Griffith

The Black Drop sank in Amsumati’s bosom,
advancing with ten thousand round about it.
Indra with might longed for it as it panted:
the hero-hearted laid aside his weapons.

Geldner

Drapsa stieg in die Amsumati hinab, Krishna ist im Anzug mit zehntausend Kriegern. Ihm stand Indra bei, dem mit aller Kraft Blasenden. Der Mannhafte wendete die Heerhaufen ab.

English translation:

тАЬ“I have seen the swift-moving (demon) lurking in an inaccessible plural ce, in the depths of the riverAс╣Г┼Ыumat─л, (I have seen) Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa standing there as (the sun) in a cloud; I appeal to you, showerers; conquerhim in battle”.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This is Indra’s speech to the Maruts. Though the demon thinks he is concealing himself, he isseen as clearly by Indra as the sun is behind a cloud

Jamison Brereton

тАЬI saw the Droplet wandering
in the oscillating eddy of the Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л River,
descending like a black cloud.
I dispatch you, bulls. Fight in the contest.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The final word in a, en─Б, is taken as en─Бс╕е by the Pp., a reading followed by Grassmann, Geldner, Oldenberg, and Lubotsky; in this interpretation it modifies or doubles (since ena- is a pronominal, not an adjectival demonstrative stem) fem. acc. pl. p├║raс╕е earlier in the p─Бda. I do not rule this out, but wonder whether it can be the enclitic instr. sg. en─Б to ay├бm in the meaning тАШin that way, i.e., howтАЩ. See en─Б тАШtherebyтАЩ in V.2.11, in addition to personal uses (тАШwith himтАЩ) in IX.96.2, X.108.3.

P─Бda b collects several words that have been prominent in the characterization of Indra earlier in the hymn: ├│jas─Б (├│jiс╣гс╣нham 10d), ┼Ыaviс╣гс╣нha (┼Ыavasas pate 6b, ┼Ы├бvas─Б 9c), and ┼Ыakra (┼Ыakra 4a). It is esp. clever that the grammatical identities of the first two terms have been switched: s-stem instr. to superlative and vice versa.

Note that though cd forms a single clause with two different subjects (тАЬall the worldsтАЭ and тАЬheaven and earthтАЭ), the dual verb rejete agrees with the nearer one, the decomposed dual dvandva dy─Б╠Бv─Б тАж pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бca.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both L├╝ders (Var. 20, 506) and Schlerath (K├╢. 139) consider this sequence to be a satyakriya. I can see the point, but if it is a truth-formulation, it is a muted one. The concept is clearest in 15a тАЬLet this truth be protective of me,тАЭ esp. since this is the last verse of the hymn. The truth-formulation itself could be either the preceding verse (so L├╝ders) or the whole hymn (Schlerath allows both possibilities). In the absence of the standard instrumental с╣Ыt├йс╣Зa (later satyena) that signals a satyakriya I am reluctant to label it as such, though certainly it is akin.

Schlerath also point out that the last word of the hymn is r─Бjan.

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the introduction, the identity of the тАШdropletтАЩ (draps├б-) and the purport of this tс╣Ыca are quite unclear. Geldner takes both draps├б- and kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├б- (тАШblackтАЩ) as PNs and the tс╣Ыca as their тАЬsaga.тАЭ Since such a saga is otherwise unknown and both words have lexical meaning, such an approach does not seem to gain us much.

OldenbergтАЩs discussion is, as usual, very sharp, but his own interpretation, that Indra is helping an embryonic version of Bс╣Ыhaspati, in the form of a drop of semen, to come to birth, also does not convince.

Schmidt (1968: 112-13) rejects OldenbergтАЩs interpretation and suggests that it describes in mystical fashion the freeing of the soma-drop in the form of the sun, but declines to tr. the tс╣Ыca because of the many uncertainties.

I am inclined to see it as a treatment of the ritual step of rinsing the soma in water, as I said in the published introduction, though much remains murky.

Griffith

I saw the Drop in the far distance moving,
on the slope bank of Amsumati’s river,
Like a black cloud that sank into the water.
Heroes, I send you forth. Go, fight in battle.

Ich sah den Drapsa in schlimmer Lage im Scho├Яe des Flusses Amsumati, ich sah den Krishna, der schwarz wie eine Wolke hinabgestiegen war. Euch, Bullen, biete ich auf: K├дmpfet im Streite!

Ich sah den Tropfen wandern in der Ferne im Niedergang des somareichen Stromes; Er kam herab wie eine schwarze Wolke, ich send’ ihn euch, o Helden, k├дmpft in Schlachten.

Then the Droplet held his body in the lap of the Aс╣Г┼Ыumat─л, as he glittered.

тАЬThe distillate of all motherтАЩs milkтАЭ for vi┼Ыv├бpsnya- assumes the etymological connection between -psnya- and st├бna- тАШbreastтАЩ, which is now standard doctrine. See EWA s.v. st├бna-.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both L├╝ders (Var. 20, 506) and Schlerath (K├╢. 139) consider this sequence to be a satyakriya. I can see the point, but if it is a truth-formulation, it is a muted one. The concept is clearest in 15a тАЬLet this truth be protective of me,тАЭ esp. since this is the last verse of the hymn. The truth-formulation itself could be either the preceding verse (so L├╝ders) or the whole hymn (Schlerath allows both possibilities). In the absence of the standard instrumental с╣Ыt├йс╣Зa (later satyena) that signals a satyakriya I am reluctant to label it as such, though certainly it is akin.

Schlerath also point out that the last word of the hymn is r─Бjan.

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the introduction, the identity of the тАШdropletтАЩ (draps├б-) and the purport of this tс╣Ыca are quite unclear. Geldner takes both draps├б- and kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├б- (тАШblackтАЩ) as PNs and the tс╣Ыca as their тАЬsaga.тАЭ Since such a saga is otherwise unknown and both words have lexical meaning, such an approach does not seem to gain us much.

OldenbergтАЩs discussion is, as usual, very sharp, but his own interpretation, that Indra is helping an embryonic version of Bс╣Ыhaspati, in the form of a drop of semen, to come to birth, also does not convince.

Schmidt (1968: 112-13) rejects OldenbergтАЩs interpretation and suggests that it describes in mystical fashion the freeing of the soma-drop in the form of the sun, but declines to tr. the tс╣Ыca because of the many uncertainties.

I am inclined to see it as a treatment of the ritual step of rinsing the soma in water, as I said in the published introduction, though much remains murky.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs soon as you were born, Indra, you were an enemy to those seven who had no enemy; yourecovered the heavens and earth when concealed (in darkness); you cause joy to the mighty worlds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thoseseven who had no enemy: Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, Vс╣Ыtra, Nam┼лci, ┼Ъambara etc.; or, you were an enemy to those who had noenemy, on behalf of the seven sages (the Aс╣Еgirasas). i.e., inorder to recover their cows

Jamison Brereton

You thenтАФjust as you were being born, you became the rival to the seven unrivaled ones, Indra.
You discovered heaven and earth, which were hidden. You provided joy to the wide-ranging creatures.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity of the тАЬsevenтАЭ is unclear; ordinarily that number refers to rivers or priestly offices, but neither makes sense here. However, Geldner (n. to 16a) points to seven enemies destroyed by Indra in X.49.8, 120.6.

Geldner takes vibhu-m├бnt- (only here) as тАШdie in dir einen Gebieter hattenтАЩ; this might be plausible, because Indra is characterized as vibh┼л╠Бin 11 and so creatures associated with him might possess him as vibh├║-. But the problem is that vibh├║-/┼л╠Б- is only adjectival, as far as I can tell, and does not have the тАШlord, masterтАЩ meaning presupposed here. Though possessive -vant-/-mant- stems should be built to nouns, Debrunner (AiG II.2.877-78) allows for pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ use of the suffix with adjectives in this and a number of other cases.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These three vss. begin tv├бс╣Г ha ty├бd. As elsewhere with this configuration (2ND SG. PRN ha ty├бd), with a neut. ty├бd without a neut. referent, ha ty├бd seems to be strongly emphatic (see a similar sequence in I.63.4-7 and comm. ad loc. as well as ad VI.18.3). I would now be inclined to change the tr. of the three vss. here to тАЬIt was just you who тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Then, at thy birth, thou wast the foeman, Indra, of those the seven who ne’er had met a rival.
The hidden Pair, the Heaven and Earth, thou foundest, and to the mighty worlds thou gavest pleasure.

Geldner

Als du geboren wurdest, wardst du der Sieben, die keinen Bemeisterer fanden, Meister, o Indra. Du fandest die versteckten Welth├дlften wieder; du brachtest den Gesch├╢pfen Freude, die in dir einen Gebieter hatten.

Grassmann

Geboren kaum, erstandest du, o Indra, als Feind den sieben, die sich feindlos d├╝nkten; Du fandest Erd’ und Himmel, die verborgnen, verschafftest Lust den machtbegabten Welten.

You thenтАФbull of the settled domains, you became the forceful bane of obstacles.
You released the rivers, which had been blocked. You conquered the
waters whose husband was a D─Бsa.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who noble in his exploits rejoices in the Soma-libations, he whose wrath cannot be repelled and whois wealthy as the days, he who alone performs the rites for his worshipper– he, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, men say, is amatch for all others.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who is wealthy as the days: wealth is produced in the days, not in the nights

Jamison Brereton

тАЬHe is the very resolute one, who is the enjoyer of the pressings, to whom the battle-fury has been conceded, who is like a rich man
through (all) the days,
who all alone is the performer of manly labors.тАЭ тАЬThatтАЩs the
Vr╠еtra-smiter!тАЭ they respond to the other.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, I interpret this verse as containing a riddle (a-c) and its answer (d), an interpretation at odds with Geldner (flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa), who takes all of the verse until its last word as part of a single description of Indra. His rendering of d, тАЬder Vс╣Ыtrat├╢ter ist (jedem) anderen gewachsen, so sagen sieтАЭ is grammatically impossible because ─Бhuс╕е ought then to be accented; pr├бt─л╠Бd any├бm ─Бhuс╕е must be a separate clause (as Oldenberg also takes it, though with implausible semantics). In my interpretation the first three p─Бdas present several different descriptions of IndraтАЩs characteristics and activities. Although these descriptions are fairly transparent, they do not name Indra, whereas the first two words of p─Бda d, s├б vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Б, names him by his standing epithet and serves as answer to the implicit riddle posed by the first three p─Бdas. Although this interpretation is more complex than GeldnerтАЩs, it allows us to account for the odd finale of d and especially for the any├бm, which by my rules (Fs. Beekes, 1997) should have a definite reading, тАЬthe other.тАЭ I take this тАЬotherтАЭ to be the poser of the riddle, and the unidentified speakers of d triumphantly respond to him with the solution. That the first two words of the final two verses of the tс╣Ыca (and the hymn) repeat s├б vс╣Ыtrah─Б╠Бof 19d, followed by the actual name of the god, lends support to my interpretation of vs. 19.

I tr. loc. sut├йс╣гu in a as if it were a genitive; тАЬenjoyer at the pressingsтАЭ would be possible, but just a little less parsable in English.

I am somewhat puzzled by the simile of b: y├│ ├бheva rev─Б╠Бn. Geldner takes the ├бh─Б (so Pp.) as the comparandum with Indra and rev─Б╠Бn as the shared quality (тАЬder wie die (neuen) Tage prangend istтАЭ), but rev├бnt- doesnтАЩt mean тАШresplendentтАЩ; rather, as a derivative of ray├н-тАШ wealthтАЩ, it means тАШrich, wealthyтАЩ. Moreover, in similes, ├бh─Б, marked by iva, several times precedes the actual comparandum and serves as adverbial qualifier - e.g., I.130.2 ├бh─Б v├н┼Ыveva s┼л╠Бryam тАЬlike the sun through all the daysтАЭ (cf. also ├бheva in VI.61.9), and so I interpret it here, though I admit it is still not a compelling image.

In c the Saс╣Гhit─Б text reads n├бry├бp─Бс╣Гsi (as also in I.85.9), with five syllables, suggesting a word separation n├бri ├бp─Бс╣Гsi and so analyzed by Pp. (followed by Aufrecht and Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition). But this must represent, one way or another, the collocation n├бry─Б + ├бp─Бс╣Гsi, found in opposite order even in this same tс╣Ыca (21c ├бp─Бс╣Гsi n├бry─Б; see also IV.19.10, as well as ├бp─Бс╣Гsi тАж n├бry─Бс╣Зi VII.21.4; also the bahuvr─лhi n├бry─Бpas- in nearby VIII.93.1). Grassmann suggests reading *n├бry─Б╠Бp─Бс╣Гsi, as does Oldenberg (ad I.85.9)(see also Macdonell Vedic Reader ad I.85.9), and this тАЬslight emendationтАЭ (MacdonellтАЩs words) not only fixes the morphology but also restores a more standard break ( ╠о ╠о _ ) for the three shorts ( ╠о ╠о ╠о) found (though the latter break is by no means uncommon). However, Lubotsky apparently takes n├бri here as the loc. to the noun nс╣Ы╠Б- (the n├бry├бp─Бс╣Гsi passages would contain the only locatives to this stem in the RV), and Geldner adduces the somewhat parallel case of vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыс╣Зi тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е (V.35.4, VIII.3.10), vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыс╣Зi pa├║с╣Гsyam (VIII.7.23). Like our n├бri ├бp─Бс╣Гsi / ├бp─Бс╣Гsi n├бry─Б, the former collocation exists alongside one with a properly formed -iyaadjective, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З(i)yaс╣Г ┼Ы├бvaс╕е (VIII.3.8 [same hymn as one of the truncated occurrences], VIII.51.10 IX.64.2). But the easy fix available to the n├бri ├бp─Бс╣Гsi case (lengthening the vowel of ├бp─Бс╣Гsi) is not available for the vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi examples.

I do not know quite what to do with all this. The vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi case looks to me like an artificial truncation that nonetheless was original to the text, while IтАЩm inclined to see n├бri as a redactional change, perhaps on the model of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi. I am thus willing to follow Grassmann, Oldenberg, and Macdonell in emending to *n├бry─Б╠Бp─Бс╣Гsi. However, these are, to say the least, quite subjective criteria, and I am not at all convinced these views are correct. It is nonetheless possible to sketch a possible but problematic scenario for these developments. The two examples of vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыс╣Зi te ┼Ы├бvaс╕е are nominal clauses. Cf. ## 10 t├бd indra vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi te ┼Ы├бvaс╕е, rendered in the published translation тАЬthat is your bullish vast power, Indra,тАЭ with vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi nominally a neut. sg. to an otherwise non-existent i-stem adj. But it might be possible instead to take it as the loc. sg. of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-, with vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е тАЬthe power is in the bull.тАЭ Though in a cursory look I have found no ┼Ы├бvaс╕е + LOC. constructions in the RV, other abstract words for power do figure in such syntagms (including in our hymn, VIII.96.3). See, e.g., V.33.6 papс╣Ыkс╣г├йс╣Зyam indra tv├й h├н ├│jaс╕е, nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni ca тАж тАЬFor, Indra, in you are strength to be nurtured and manly powers.тАЭ There are two fundamental problems with this suggestion: 1) the zero-grade loc. -ni to -an-stems is not found in the RV; we find only full-grade -ani; 2) it is hard to construe the te, since the bull and 2nd ps. Indra are coreferential. тАЬThis power of yours is in (you,) the bullтАЭ is awkward and unlikely. A bolder hypothesis - bolder than I would venture - would link these two problems and reconstruct an underlying syntagm *vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зi ┼Ы├бvaс╕е with full-grade loc. and no enclitic pronoun. When the posited vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зi reduced to vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi (perhaps because of association with adjectival vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З(i)ya-), te was introduced to maintain the metrical shape. There are no other attested examples of the loc. sg. of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- in the RV to support the trisyllabic reading. In any case, in this scenario the old loc. would be reinterpreted as an endingless adjectival or adverbial element in this collocation, alternating with syntactically impeccable vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З(i)yaс╣Г ┼Ы├бvaс╕е. With this set up, we can get n├бri on this model: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З(i)yaс╣Г ┼Ы├бvaс╕е : vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыс╣Зi тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е ├бp─Бс╣Гsi n├бry─Б : n├бri ├бp─Бс╣Гsi I believe this development was redactional rather than found in the ur-text. First because vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыс╣Зi тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е is a plausible neut. sg. phrase, but with the pl. ├бp─Бс╣Гsi an endingless n├бri is more difficult. Moreover, an abstract quality located in a being (like тАЬstrength is in the bullтАЭ) is a much more likely notion than тАЬlabors are in the man.тАЭ And the metrical evidence strongly favors an original *n├бry─Б╠Бp─Бс╣Гsi, though it does not entirely rule out the short vowel.

But I lay out this scenario very skeptically, primarily because of the wrong grade in the posited loc. sg. Here I would point out that the same trouble would afflict any attempt to explain vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З(i)ya- as a thematic descasuative derivative from a locative by pointing to the two synchronically alternating syntagms here. Such a derivation for *-(i)yo-possessive adjectives in general has been proposed (see Balles, Sprache 39 [1997 (2000)] 141-67, cited from Meier-Br├╝gger, Indo-European Linguistics, 283-84, for which ref. I thank Jesse Lundquist). I do not believe that the last word has been said about this issue.

Griffith

Most wise is he, rejoicing in libations, splendid as day, resistless in his anger.
He only doth great deeds, the only Hero, sole Vrtra-slayer he, with none beside him.

Wilson
